Fix 1 PR206 issue in /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/memory/consolidate.ts:

**Orphan cleanup race if crash between phases**: PR #206 added orphan cleanup for `msg_terms` and `code_symbols` after pruning short-term memory. The issue is: if the process crashes between deleting memories and deleting their orphaned terms/symbols, the orphans remain permanently.

Fix: Wrap the orphan cleanup in a try/catch so that a failure in orphan cleanup doesn't crash the pruning function, and add a comment explaining the race:

```typescript
// Orphan cleanup: best-effort, non-fatal
// If process crashes between memory deletion and orphan cleanup,
// orphans will accumulate but won't cause data corruption
try {
  // ... existing orphan deletion code ...
} catch (orphanErr) {
  console.warn('Non-fatal: orphan cleanup failed:', orphanErr)
}
```

Fix 1 PR206 issue in /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/app/page.tsx:

**toggleSidebar setTimeout not cleaned up**: The `toggleSidebar` function uses `setTimeout(() => window.dispatchEvent(new Event('resize')), 350)` but doesn't store the timeout ID. While this is LOW severity (the callback is a no-op if component unmounted), clean it up properly.

Since `toggleSidebar` is called on button click (not in a useEffect), the simplest fix is to store the timeout in a ref and clear it on component unmount. Look at the component to see if there's already a ref or useEffect that handles cleanup on unmount. If so, add `clearTimeout(resizeTimeoutRef.current)` there. If not, add:

```typescript
const resizeTimeoutRef = useRef<ReturnType<typeof setTimeout> | null>(null)
```

And in `toggleSidebar`:
```typescript
if (resizeTimeoutRef.current) clearTimeout(resizeTimeoutRef.current)
resizeTimeoutRef.current = setTimeout(() => {
  window.dispatchEvent(new Event('resize'))
}, 350)
```

    10→
    11→## BUG-1: Scroll handlers fire on BOTH keydown AND keyup (DOUBLE-SCROLL)
    12→
    13→**Severity: HIGH** -- Users experience double-scrolling on every scroll keystroke.
    14→
    15→**Location:** `hooks/useTerminal.ts` lines 204-233
    16→
    17→**Problem:** The six scroll key handlers (Shift+PageUp/Down, Shift+ArrowUp/Down, Shift+Home/End) do NOT filter by `event.type === 'keydown'`. The xterm.js `attachCustomKeyEventHandler` callback fires for BOTH `keydown` and `keyup` events. This means every scroll key press triggers the scroll action TWICE (once on key press, once on key release).
    18→
    19→The Cmd+C and Cmd+V handlers correctly filter with `if (event.type === 'keydown')` (lines 238, 252), but the scroll handlers omit this check.
    20→
    21→**Evidence:** The xterm.js type definition at `node_modules/@xterm/xterm/typings/xterm.d.ts:1060-1069` shows the official example explicitly filtering by `ev.type === 'keydown'`.
    22→
    23→**Fix:** Add `event.type === 'keydown'` guard to each scroll handler:
    24→```typescript
    25→// Before (BUGGY):
    26→if (event.shiftKey && event.key === 'PageUp') {
    27→  terminal.scrollLines(-scrollAmount)
    28→  return false
    29→}
    30→
    31→// After (FIXED):
    32→if (event.type === 'keydown' && event.shiftKey && event.key === 'PageUp') {
    33→  terminal.scrollLines(-scrollAmount)
    34→  return false
    35→}
    36→```
    37→
    38→Apply the same fix to all six scroll handlers (PageUp, PageDown, ArrowUp, ArrowDown, Home, End).
    39→
    40→---
    41→
    42→## LATENT-1: Cmd+C with selection -- clipboard failure does NOT fall through to SIGINT
    43→
    44→**Se

     9→Fresh line-by-line audit of the entire file. Found **17 issues** ranging from race conditions to logic errors and silent data corruption risks.
    10→
    11→---
    12→
    13→## CRITICAL Issues (data loss / race conditions)
    14→
    15→### C1. TOCTOU Race in `loadAgents()` Cache (Lines 148-181)
    16→
    17→**Bug:** The mtime-based cache has a classic Time-of-Check-to-Time-of-Use (TOCTOU) race.
    18→
    19→```
    20→Thread A: statSync → mtimeMs = 100
    21→Thread B: writes file → mtimeMs = 200
    22→Thread A: readFileSync → reads NEW data
    23→Thread A: _cachedMtimeMs = 100 (stale mtime stored!)
    24→Thread C: statSync → mtimeMs = 200 ≠ 100, re-reads unnecessarily
    25→```
    26→
    27→But worse: if two requests hit within the same filesystem timestamp granularity (some FS have 1-second mtime resolution), concurrent writes can produce:
    28→
    29→```
    30→Thread A: loadAgents() → reads [a, b, c]
    31→Thread B: loadAgents() → reads [a, b, c] (cache hit, same mtime)
    32→Thread A: modifies agent a, calls saveAgents([a', b, c])
    33→Thread B: modifies agent b, calls saveAgents([a, b', c]) ← OVERWRITES Thread A's change to a!
    34→```
    35→
    36→**Impact:** Every function that does `loadAgents() → modify → saveAgents()` is vulnerable. This is a read-modify-write race condition. Functions affected: `updateAgent`, `updateAgentMetrics`, `incrementAgentMetric`, `linkSession`, `unlinkSession`, `createAgent`, `deleteAgent`, `renameAgent`, `addEmailAddress`, `removeEmailAddress`, `addAMPAddress`, `removeAMPAddress`, `addMarketplaceSkills`, `removeMarketplaceSkills`, `addCustomSkill`, `removeCustomSkill`, `updateAiMaestroSkills`, `markAgentAsAMPRegistered`, `normalizeAllAgentHostIds`, `updateAgentWorkingDirectory`, and others.

    15→
    16→**File:** `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/cozo-utils.ts`, line 21
    17→**Code:** `if (!s) return 'null'`
    18→
    19→The empty string `""` is falsy in JavaScript, so `escapeForCozo("")` returns the CozoDB literal `null` instead of an empty string `''`. This means if any memory content, context, category, or other field is an empty string, it will be silently stored as `null` in CozoDB.
    20→
    21→**Impact:** If an LLM provider returns a memory with `context: ""`, it gets stored as `null`. This is unlikely to cause crashes (nullable columns handle null), but it means data is silently lost. The `context` column in the `memories` schema is `String?` (nullable), so this won't crash, but it corrupts data semantics.
    22→
    23→**Fix:** Change to `if (s === undefined || s === null) return 'null'` or `if (s == null) return 'null'`.
    24→
    25→---
    26→
    27→### BUG 2 (LOW): `escapeForCozo` does not handle NUL bytes (`\0`)
    28→
    29→**File:** `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/cozo-utils.ts`, lines 20-30
    30→
    31→CozoDB strings are stored internally and NUL bytes (`\0`) could cause truncation or parsing issues in the CozoDB query parser. The function does not strip or escape `\0` characters.
    32→
    33→**Impact:** Low probability -- LLM-extracted memories are unlikely to contain NUL bytes. But if conversation text fr

... [16851 more chars truncated]

Aborting."). This is a **false negative** that would prevent non-interactive updates from working.

     8→### BUG 1 (MEDIUM): Singleton race condition on failure — second caller gets cached rejection

    10→**Location:** Lines 24-58, `getExtractor()`
    11→
    12→**The pattern:**
    13→```typescript
    14→let extractor: FeatureExtractionPipeline | null = null;
    15→let extractorPromise: Promise<FeatureExtractionPipeline> | null = null;
    16→
    17→async function getExtractor() {

    19→  if (extractorPromise) return extractorPromise;  // <-- PROBLEM
    20→
    21→  extractorPromise = (async () => { ... })().catch((err) => {
    22→    extractor = null;
    23→    extractorPromise = null;
    24→    throw err;
    25→  });
    26→
    27→  return extractorPromise;
    28→}
    29→```
    30→
    31→**The race condition:**
    32→1. Caller A invokes `getExtractor()`. `extractorPromise` is set to the loading promise.
    33→2. Caller B invokes `getExtractor()` while model is still loading. It hits line 28: `if (extractorPromise) return extractorPromise;` — it gets the SAME promise.
    34→3. The model fails to load. The `.catch()` handler runs: resets `extractor = null`, `extractorPromise = null`, then re-throws.
    35→4. **Both** caller A and caller B receive the rejection. This is CORRECT behavior.
    36→5. Caller C arrives AFTER the `.catch()` has reset the variables. It retries. This is also CORRECT.
    37→
    38→**Verdict: NOT a bug.** The `.catch()` handler properly resets both variables before re-throwing. The re-throw happens synchronously within the `.catch()`, and since `extractorPromise` is nulled inside `.catch()` (which runs before the re-throw propagates), any caller arriving after the failure will retry. Callers who received the same promise will all get the rejection, which is

    12→
    13→**Severity: HIGH** -- Users experience double-scrolling on every scroll keystroke.
    14→
    15→**Location:** `hooks/useTerminal.ts` lines 204-233
    16→
    17→**Problem:** The six scroll key handlers (Shift+PageUp/Down, Shift+ArrowUp/Down, Shift+Home/End) do NOT filter by `event.type === 'keydown'`. The xterm.js `attachCustomKeyEventHandler` callback fires for BOTH `keydown` and `keyup` events. This means every scroll key press triggers the scroll action TWICE (once on key press, once on key release).
    18→
    19→The Cmd+C and Cmd+V handlers correctly filter with `if (event.type === 'keydown')` (lines 238, 252), but the scroll handlers omit this check.
    20→
    21→**Evidence:** The xterm.js type definition at `node_modules/@xterm/xterm/typings/xterm.d.ts:1060-1069` shows the official example explicitly filtering by `ev.type === 'keydown'`.
    22→
    23→**Fix:** Add `event.type === 'keydown'` guard to each scroll handler:
    24→```typescript
    25→// Before (BUGGY):
    26→if (event.shiftKey && event.key === 'PageUp') {
    27→  terminal.scrollLines(-scrollAmount)
    28→  return false
    29→}
    30→
    31→// After (FIXED):
    32→if (event.type === 'keydown' && event.shiftKey && event.key === 'PageUp') {
    33→  terminal.scrollLines(-scrollAmount)
    34→  return false
    35→}
    36→```
    37→
    38→Apply the same fix to all six scroll handlers (PageUp, PageDown, ArrowUp, ArrowDown, Home, End).

    10→

    12→
    13→## CRITICAL Issues (data loss / race conditions)
    14→
    15→### C1. TOCTOU Race in `loadAgents()` Cache (Lines 148-181)
    16→
    17→**Bug:** The mtime-based cache has a classic Time-of-Check-to-Time-of-Use (TOCTOU) race.
    18→
    19→```
    20→Thread A: statSync → mtimeMs = 100
    21→Thread B: writes file → mtimeMs = 200
    22→Thread A: readFileSync → reads NEW data
    23→Thread A: _cachedMtimeMs = 100 (stale mtime stored!)
    24→Thread C: statSync → mtimeMs = 200 ≠ 100, re-reads unnecessarily
    25→```
    26→
    27→But worse: if two requests hit within the same filesystem timestamp granularity (some FS have 1-second mtime resolution), concurrent writes can produce:
    28→
    29→```
    30→Thread A: loadAgents() → reads [a, b, c]
    31→Thread B: loadAgents() → reads [a, b, c] (cache hit, same mtime)
    32→Thread A: modifies agent a, calls saveAgents([a', b, c])
    33→Thread B: modifies agent b, calls saveAgents([a, b', c]) ← OVERWRITES Thread A's change to a!
    34→```
    35→
    36→**Impact:** Every function that does `loadAgents() → modify → saveAgents()` is vulnerable. This is a read-modify-write race condition. Functions affected: `updateAgent`, `updateAgentMetrics`, `incrementAgentMetric`, `linkSession`, `unlinkSession`, `createAgent`, `deleteAgent`, `renameAgent`, `addEmailAddress`, `removeEmailAddress`, `addAMPAddress`, `removeAMPAddress`, `addMarketplaceSkills`, `removeMarketplaceSkills`, `addCustomSkill`, `removeCustomSkill`, `updateAiMaestroSkills`, `markAgentAsAMPRegistered`, `normalizeAllAgentHostIds`, `updateAgentWorkingDirectory`, and others.

    15→

    17→**Code:** `if (!s) return 'null'`
    18→
    19→The empty string `""` is falsy in JavaScript, so `escapeForCozo("")` returns the CozoDB literal `null` instead of an empty string `''`. This means if any memory content, context, category, or other field is an empty string, it will be silently stored as `null` in CozoDB.
    20→
    21→**Impact:** If an LLM provider returns a memory with `context: ""`, it gets stored as `null`. This is unlikely to cause crashes (nullable columns handle null), but it means data is silently lost. The `context` column in the `memories` schema is `String?` (nullable), so this won't crash, but it corrupts data semantics.
    22→
    23→**Fix:** Change to `if (s === undefined || s === null) return 'null'` or `if (s == null) return 'null'`.
    24→
    25→---
    26→
    27→### BUG 2 (LOW): `escapeForCozo` does not handle NUL bytes (`\0`)
    28→
    29→**File:** `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/cozo-utils.ts`, lines 20-30
    30→
    31→CozoDB strings are stored internally and NUL bytes (`\0`) could cause truncation or parsing issues in the CozoDB query parser. The function does not strip or escape `\0` characters.
    32→
    33→**Impact:** Low probability -- LLM-extracted memories are unlikely to contain NUL bytes. But if conversation text fr

... [16851 more chars truncated]

+  const createHnswIndexIfNotExists = async (db: AgentDatabase, ddl: string) => {

+      await db.run(ddl)

     1→# Third-Pass Deep Audit: DeleteAgentDialog.tsx
     2→Generated: 2026-02-15
     3→
     4→File: `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/components/DeleteAgentDialog.tsx` (411 lines)
     5→
     6→---
     7→
     8→## 1. Export Handler: Network Error Handling
     9→
    10→**Lines 65-93**
    11→
    12→The `try/catch/finally` structure is correctly set up. If `fetch()` throws a network error (e.g., DNS failure, network offline, CORS error), execution jumps to the `catch` block at line 88. The catch block IS reached.
    13→
    14→**However**, there is a subtle issue at line 71-72:
    15→
    16→```typescript
    17→const errBody = await res.text()
    18→throw new Error(errBody || `Export failed (${res.status})`)
    19→```
    20→
    21→If `res.text()` itself throws (e.g., the response stream was aborted mid-flight), this error will propagate to the outer `catch` block, which is fine. But the error message will be the stream error, not the HTTP status. This is a minor diagnostic issue, not a bug.
    22→
    23→**VERDICT: No bug.** Catch block is correctly reached for all fetch errors.
    24→
    25→---
    26→
    27→## 2. response.blob() Failure / Empty Blob
    28→
    29→**Line 75**: `const blob = await res.blob()`
    30→
    31→If `res.blob()` throws (stream error, aborted connection), the catch block handles it correctly.
    32→
    33→**If the blob is empty (0 bytes):**
    34→- `URL.createObjectURL(blob)` will succeed -- it creates a valid object URL for an empty blob.

    16→
    17→**Problem:** The six scroll key handlers (Shift+PageUp/Down, Shift+ArrowUp/Down, Shift+Home/End) do NOT filter by `event.type === 'keydown'`.     22→

    24→```typescript
    25→// Before (BUGGY):
    26→if (event.shiftKey && event.key === 'PageUp') {
    27→  terminal.scrollLines(-scrollAmount)
    28→  return false
    29→}
    30→
    31→// After (FIXED):
    32→if (event.type === 'keydown' && event.shiftKey && event.key === 'PageUp') {
    33→  terminal.scrollLines(-scrollAmount)
    34→  return false
    35→}
    36→```
    37→
    38→Apply the same fix to all six scroll handlers (PageUp, PageDown, ArrowUp, ArrowDown, Home, End).

     7→## Summary

     9→Fresh line-by-line audit of the entire file. Found **17 issues** ranging from race conditions to logic errors and silent data corruption risks.
    10→
    11→---
    12→
    13→## CRITICAL Issues (data loss / race conditions)
    14→
    15→### C1. TOCTOU Race in `loadAgents()` Cache (Lines 148-181)
    16→
    17→**Bug:** The mtime-based cache has a classic Time-of-Check-to-Time-of-Use (TOCTOU) race.
    18→
    19→```
    20→Thread A: statSync → mtimeMs = 100
    21→Thread B: writes file → mtimeMs = 200
    22→Thread A: readFileSync → reads NEW data
    23→Thread A: _cachedMtimeMs = 100 (stale mtime stored!)
    24→Thread C: statSync → mtimeMs = 200 ≠ 100, re-reads unnecessarily
    25→```
    26→
    27→But worse: if two requests hit within the same filesystem timestamp granularity (some FS have 1-second mtime resolution), concurrent writes can produce:
    28→
    29→```
    30→Thread A: loadAgents() → reads [a, b, c]
    31→Thread B: loadAgents() → reads [a, b, c] (cache hit, same mtime)
    32→Thread A: modifies agent a, calls saveAgents([a', b, c])
    33→Thread B: modifies agent b, calls saveAgents([a, b', c]) ← OVERWRITES Thread A's change to a!
    34→```
    35→
    36→**Impact:** Every function that does `loadAgents() → modify → saveAgents()` is vulnerable. This is a read-modify-write race condition. Functions affected: `updateAgent`, `updateAgentMetrics`, `incrementAgentMetric`, `linkSession`, `unlinkSession`, `createAgent`, `deleteAgent`, `renameAgent`, `addEmailAddress`, `removeEmailAddress`, `addAMPAddress`, `removeAMPAddress`, `addMarketplaceSkills`, `removeMarketplaceSkills`, `addCustomSkill`, `removeCustomSkill`, `updateAiMaestroSkills`, `markAgentAsAMPRegistered`, `normalizeAllAgentHostIds`, `updateAgentWorkingDirectory`, and others.

     5→
     6→---
     7→
     8→### BUG 1 (MEDIUM): Singleton race condition on failure — second caller gets cached rejection
     9→
    10→**Location:** Lines 24-58, `getExtractor()`
    11→
    12→**The pattern:**
    13→```typescript
    14→let extractor: FeatureExtractionPipeline | null = null;
    15→let extractorPromise: Promise<FeatureExtractionPipeline> | null = null;
    16→
    17→async function getExtractor() {
    18→  if (extractor) return extractor;
    19→  if (extractorPromise) return extractorPromise;  // <-- PROBLEM
    20→
    21→  extractorPromise = (async () => { ... })().catch((err) => {
    22→    extractor = null;
    23→    extractorPromise = null;
    24→    throw err;
    25→  });
    26→
    27→  return extractorPromise;
    28→}
    29→```
    30→
    31→**The race condition:**
    32→1. Caller A invokes `getExtractor()`. `extractorPromise` is set to the loading promise.
    33→2. Caller B invokes `getExtractor()` while model is still loading. It hits line 28: `if (extractorPromise) return extractorPromise;` — it gets the SAME promise.
    34→3. The model fails to load. The `.catch()` handler runs: resets `extractor = null`, `extractorPromise = null`, then re-throws.
    35→4. **Both** caller A and caller B receive the rejection. This is CORRECT behavior.
    36→5. Caller C arrives AFTER the `.catch()` has reset the variables. It retries. This is also CORRECT.
    37→
    38→**Verdict: NOT a bug.** The `.catch()` handler properly resets both variables before re-throwing. The re-throw happens synchronously within the `.catch()`, and since `extractorPromise` is nulled inside `.catch()` (which runs before the re-throw propagates), any caller arriving after the failure will retry. Callers who received the same promise will all get the rejection, which is

... [19271 more chars truncated]

</details>

    25→```
    26→This checks for the exact string `"name": "ai-maestro"` -- but JSON allows whitespace variations like `"name" : "ai-maestro"` or `"name":"ai-maestro"`. Aborting."). This is a **false negative** that would prevent non-interactive updates from working.

     7→## Summary
     8→
     9→Fresh line-by-line audit of the entire file. Found **17 issues** ranging from race conditions to logic errors and silent data corruption risks.
    10→
    11→---
    12→
    13→## CRITICAL Issues (data loss / race conditions)
    14→
    15→### C1. TOCTOU Race in `loadAgents()` Cache (Lines 148-181)
    16→
    17→**Bug:** The mtime-based cache has a classic Time-of-Check-to-Time-of-Use (TOCTOU) race.
    18→
    19→```
    20→Thread A: statSync → mtimeMs = 100
    21→Thread B: writes file → mtimeMs = 200
    22→Thread A: readFileSync → reads NEW data
    23→Thread A: _cachedMtimeMs = 100 (stale mtime stored!)
    24→Thread C: statSync → mtimeMs = 200 ≠ 100, re-reads unnecessarily
    25→```
    26→
    27→But worse: if two requests hit within the same filesystem timestamp granularity (some FS have 1-second mtime resolution), concurrent writes can produce:
    28→
    29→```
    30→Thread A: loadAgents() → reads [a, b, c]
    31→Thread B: loadAgents() → reads [a, b, c] (cache hit, same mtime)
    32→Thread A: modifies agent a, calls saveAgents([a', b, c])
    33→Thread B: modifies agent b, calls saveAgents([a, b', c]) ← OVERWRITES Thread A's change to a!
    34→```
    35→
    36→**Impact:** Every function that does `loadAgents() → modify → saveAgents()` is vulnerable. This is a read-modify-write race condition. Functions affected: `updateAgent`, `updateAgentMetrics`, `incrementAgentMetric`, `linkSession`, `unlinkSession`, `createAgent`, `deleteAgent`, `renameAgent`, `addEmailAddress`, `removeEmailAddress`, `addAMPAddress`, `removeAMPAddress`, `addMarketplaceSkills`, `removeMarketplaceSkills`, `addCustomSkill`, `removeCustomSkill`, `updateAiMaestroSkills`, `markAgentAsAMPRegistered`, `normalizeAllAgentHostIds`, `updateAgentWorkingDirectory`, and others.

    12→
    13→**Severity: HIGH** -- Users experience double-scrolling on every scroll keystroke.
    14→
    15→**Location:** `hooks/useTerminal.ts` lines 204-233
    16→
    17→**Problem:** The six scroll key handlers (Shift+PageUp/Down, Shift+ArrowUp/Down, Shift+Home/End) do NOT filter by `event.type === 'keydown'`. The xterm.js `attachCustomKeyEventHandler` callback fires for BOTH `keydown` and `keyup` events. This means every scroll key press triggers the scroll action TWICE (once on key press, once on key release).
    18→

    20→
    21→**Evidence:** The xterm.js type definition at `node_modules/@xterm/xterm/typings/xterm.d.ts:1060-1069` shows the official example explicitly filtering by `ev.type === 'keydown'`.
    22→
    23→**Fix:** Add `event.type === 'keydown'` guard to each scroll handler:
    24→```typescript
    25→// Before (BUGGY):
    26→if (event.shiftKey && event.key === 'PageUp') {
    27→  terminal.scrollLines(-scrollAmount)
    28→  return false
    29→}
    30→
    31→// After (FIXED):
    32→if (event.type === 'keydown' && event.shiftKey && event.key === 'PageUp') {
    33→  terminal.scrollLines(-scrollAmount)
    34→  return false
    35→}
    36→```
    37→
    38→Apply the same fix to all six scroll handlers (PageUp, PageDown, ArrowUp, ArrowDown, Home, End).

If CozoDB changes the error message wording in a future version (e.g., to "index already defined", "duplicate index", or a localized message), this would fail to catch the "already exists" case and would throw, crashing schema initialization.
    31→- **cozo-node version:** `^0.7.6` (from package.json). The `^` semver range means minor/patch upgrades are allowed, and error message wording is NOT part of semver guarantees.
    32→
    33→**Severity: MEDIUM**

    15→
    16→**File:** `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/cozo-utils.ts`, line 21
    17→**Code:** `if (!s) return 'null'`
    18→
    19→The empty string `""` is falsy in JavaScript, so `escapeForCozo("")` returns the CozoDB literal `null` instead of an empty string `''`. This means if any memory content, context, category, or other field is an empty string, it will be silently stored as `null` in CozoDB.
    20→
    21→**Impact:** If an LLM provider returns a memory with `context: ""`, it gets stored as `null`. This is unlikely to cause crashes (nullable columns handle null), but it means data is silently lost. The `context` column in the `memories` schema is `String?` (nullable), so this won't crash, but it corrupts data semantics.
    22→
    23→**Fix:** Change to `if (s === undefined || s === null) return 'null'` or `if (s == null) return 'null'`.
    24→
    25→---
    26→
    27→### BUG 2 (LOW): `escapeForCozo` does not handle NUL bytes (`\0`)

    30→
    31→CozoDB strings are stored internally and NUL bytes (`\0`) could cause truncation or parsing issues in the CozoDB query parser. The function does not strip or escape `\0` characters.

    33→**Impact:** Low probability -- LLM-extracted memories are unlikely to contain NUL bytes. But if conversation text fr

... [16851 more chars truncated]

     5→
     6→---
     7→
     8→### BUG 1 (MEDIUM): Singleton race condition on failure — second caller gets cached rejection
     9→
    10→**Location:** Lines 24-58, `getExtractor()`
    11→
    12→**The pattern:**
    13→```typescript
    14→let extractor: FeatureExtractionPipeline | null = null;
    15→let extractorPromise: Promise<FeatureExtractionPipeline> | null = null;
    16→
    17→async function getExtractor() {
    18→  if (extractor) return extractor;
    19→  if (extractorPromise) return extractorPromise;  // <-- PROBLEM
    20→
    21→  extractorPromise = (async () => { ... })().catch((err) => {
    22→    extractor = null;
    23→    extractorPromise = null;
    24→    throw err;
    25→  });
    26→
    27→  return extractorPromise;
    28→}
    29→```
    30→
    31→**The race condition:**
    32→1. Caller A invokes `getExtractor()`. `extractorPromise` is set to the loading promise.
    33→2. Caller B invokes `getExtractor()` while model is still loading. It hits line 28: `if (extractorPromise) return extractorPromise;` — it gets the SAME promise.
    34→3. The model fails to load. The `.catch()` handler runs: resets `extractor = null`, `extractorPromise = null`, then re-throws.
    35→4. **Both** caller A and caller B receive the rejection. This is CORRECT behavior.
    36→5. Caller C arrives AFTER the `.catch()` has reset the variables. It retries. This is also CORRECT.
    37→
    38→**Verdict: NOT a bug.** The `.catch()` handler properly resets both variables before re-throwing. The re-throw happens synchronously within the `.catch()`, and since `extractorPromise` is nulled inside `.catch()` (which runs before the re-throw propagates), any caller arriving after the failure will retry. Callers who received the same promise will all get the rejection, which is

... [19271 more chars truncated]

    18→**Verdict: SAFE (with minor concern)**
    19→
    20→The `[ -f "package.json" ]` guard short-circuits before grep runs if the file does not exist. The `2>/dev/null` suppresses any grep errors (binary file, permission denied, etc.).     21→

    23→```bash
    24→if [ -f "$INSTALL_DIR/package.json" ] && grep -q '"name": "ai-maestro"' "$INSTALL_DIR/package.json" 2>/dev/null; then
    25→```
    26→This checks for the exact string `"name": "ai-maestro"` -- but JSON allows whitespace variations like `"name" : "ai-maestro"` or `"name":"ai-maestro"`. A minified or reformatted package.json would fail this check, causing the script to refuse to auto-replace an existing AI Maestro installation (falling through to "Directory exists but is not an AI Maestro installation. Aborting."). This is a **false negative** that would prevent non-interactive updates from working.
    27→
    28→**Severity:** MEDIUM -- affects `--from-remote` and `--non-interactive` flows if package.json formatting differs.

     6→---
     7→
     8→### BUG 1 (MEDIUM): Singleton race condition on failure — second caller gets cached rejection
     9→
    10→**Location:** Lines 24-58, `getExtractor()`
    11→
    12→**The pattern:**
    13→```typescript
    14→let extractor: FeatureExtractionPipeline | null = null;
    15→let extractorPromise: Promise<FeatureExtractionPipeline> | null = null;
    16→
    17→async function getExtractor() {
    18→  if (extractor) return extractor;
    19→  if (extractorPromise) return extractorPromise;  // <-- PROBLEM
    20→
    21→  extractorPromise = (async () => { ... })().catch((err) => {
    22→    extractor = null;
    23→    extractorPromise = null;
    24→    throw err;
    25→  });
    26→
    27→  return extractorPromise;
    28→}
    29→```
    30→
    31→**The race condition:**
    32→1. Caller A invokes `getExtractor()`. `extractorPromise` is set to the loading promise.
    33→2. Caller B invokes `getExtractor()` while model is still loading. It hits line 28: `if (extractorPromise) return extractorPromise;` — it gets the SAME promise.
    34→3. The model fails to load. The `.catch()` handler runs: resets `extractor = null`, `extractorPromise = null`, then re-throws.
    35→4. **Both** caller A and caller B receive the rejection. This is CORRECT behavior.
    36→5. Caller C arrives AFTER the `.catch()` has reset the variables. It retries. This is also CORRECT.
    37→
    38→**Verdict: NOT a bug.** The `.catch()` handler properly resets both variables before re-throwing. The re-throw happens synchronously within the `.catch()`, and since `extractorPromise` is nulled inside `.catch()` (which runs before the re-throw propagates), any caller arriving after the failure will retry. Callers who received the same promise will all get the rejection, which is

... [19271 more chars truncated]

     9→Fresh line-by-line audit of the entire file. Found **17 issues** ranging from race conditions to logic errors and silent data corruption risks.
    10→
    11→---
    12→
    13→## CRITICAL Issues (data loss / race conditions)
    14→
    15→### C1. TOCTOU Race in `loadAgents()` Cache (Lines 148-181)
    16→
    17→**Bug:** The mtime-based cache has a classic Time-of-Check-to-Time-of-Use (TOCTOU) race.
    18→
    19→```
    20→Thread A: statSync → mtimeMs = 100
    21→Thread B: writes file → mtimeMs = 200
    22→Thread A: readFileSync → reads NEW data
    23→Thread A: _cachedMtimeMs = 100 (stale mtime stored!)
    24→Thread C: statSync → mtimeMs = 200 ≠ 100, re-reads unnecessarily
    25→```
    26→
    27→But worse: if two requests hit within the same filesystem timestamp granularity (some FS have 1-second mtime resolution), concurrent writes can produce:
    28→
    29→```
    30→Thread A: loadAgents() → reads [a, b, c]
    31→Thread B: loadAgents() → reads [a, b, c] (cache hit, same mtime)
    32→Thread A: modifies agent a, calls saveAgents([a', b, c])
    33→Thread B: modifies agent b, calls saveAgents([a, b', c]) ← OVERWRITES Thread A's change to a!
    34→```
    35→
    36→**Impact:** Every function that does `loadAgents() → modify → saveAgents()` is vulnerable. This is a read-modify-write race condition. Functions affected: `updateAgent`, `updateAgentMetrics`, `incrementAgentMetric`, `linkSession`, `unlinkSession`, `createAgent`, `deleteAgent`, `renameAgent`, `addEmailAddress`, `removeEmailAddress`, `addAMPAddress`, `removeAMPAddress`, `addMarketplaceSkills`, `removeMarketplaceSkills`, `addCustomSkill`, `removeCustomSkill`, `updateAiMaestroSkills`, `markAgentAsAMPRegistered`, `normalizeAllAgentHostIds`, `updateAgentWorkingDirectory`, and others.


... [15884 more chars truncated]

    10→
    11→## BUG-1: Scroll handlers fire on BOTH keydown AND keyup (DOUBLE-SCROLL)
    12→
    13→**Severity: HIGH** -- Users experience double-scrolling on every scroll keystroke.
    14→
    15→**Location:** `hooks/useTerminal.ts` lines 204-233
    16→
    17→**Problem:** The six scroll key handlers (Shift+PageUp/Down, Shift+ArrowUp/Down, Shift+Home/End) do NOT filter by `event.type === 'keydown'`. The xterm.js `attachCustomKeyEventHandler` callback fires for BOTH `keydown` and `keyup` events. This means every scroll key press triggers the scroll action TWICE (once on key press, once on key release).
    18→
    19→The Cmd+C and Cmd+V handlers correctly filter with `if (event.type === 'keydown')` (lines 238, 252), but the scroll handlers omit this check.
    20→
    21→**Evidence:** The xterm.js type definition at `node_modules/@xterm/xterm/typings/xterm.d.ts:1060-1069` shows the official example explicitly filtering by `ev.type === 'keydown'`.
    22→
    23→**Fix:** Add `event.type === 'keydown'` guard to each scroll handler:
    24→```typescript
    25→// Before (BUGGY):
    26→if (event.shiftKey && event.key === 'PageUp') {
    27→  terminal.scrollLines(-scrollAmount)
    28→  return false
    29→}
    30→
    31→// After (FIXED):
    32→if (event.type === 'keydown' && event.shiftKey && event.key === 'PageUp') {
    33→  terminal.scrollLines(-scrollAmount)
    34→  return false
    35→}
    36→```
    37→
    38→Apply the same fix to all six scroll handlers (PageUp, PageDown, ArrowUp, ArrowDown, Home, End).

    17→**Code:** `if (!s) return 'null'`
    18→
    19→The empty string `""` is falsy in JavaScript, so `escapeForCozo("")` returns the CozoDB literal `null` instead of an empty string `''`. This means if any memory content, context, category, or other field is an empty string, it will be silently stored as `null` in CozoDB.
    20→
    21→**Impact:** If an LLM provider returns a memory with `context: ""`, it gets stored as `null`. This is unlikely to cause crashes (nullable columns handle null), but it means data is silently lost. The `context` column in the `memories` schema is `String?` (nullable), so this won't crash, but it corrupts data semantics.
    22→
    23→**Fix:** Change to `if (s === undefined || s === null) return 'null'` or `if (s == null) return 'null'`.
    24→
    25→---
    26→

**Issue 2 (lines 741-748):** Same pattern for `OTHER_SKILLS` loop. Backup guards the `rm -rf` but the `cp -r` at line 748 runs unconditionally.
